<div id="review_2128676821" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2128676821" />
    <a title="Auntie Terror" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/63716836-auntie-terror"><img alt="Auntie Terror" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593886534p2/63716836.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2128676821?book_show_action=true">Jul 02, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Auntie Terror" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Auntie Terror" href="/user/show/63716836-auntie-terror">Auntie Terror</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781473621473" href="/book/show/30965619-a-closed-and-common-orbit">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/63716836-auntie-terror?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer2128676821&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2128676821" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11695081910979998278">What would happen if you gave an AI a body? <br/><br/>This is the question which basically is at the heart of this book when deceased Lovey's new installation Lovelace is downloaded into the artificial body once supposed to hold Lovey's consciousness and taken to Port Coriol by Pepper. <br/>In this case, the AI, now an illegal entity, isn't happy and excited about it. Sidra, as she now calls herself, is frightened, insecure, and even angry because she was ripped out of what she felt was her place. At first, sh</span>
  <span id="freeText11695081910979998278" style="display:none">What would happen if you gave an AI a body? <br /><br />This is the question which basically is at the heart of this book when deceased Lovey's new installation Lovelace is downloaded into the artificial body once supposed to hold Lovey's consciousness and taken to Port Coriol by Pepper. <br />In this case, the AI, now an illegal entity, isn't happy and excited about it. Sidra, as she now calls herself, is frightened, insecure, and even angry because she was ripped out of what she felt was her place. At first, she is sure she'll never fit in - and falls into something very closely resembling puberty. But then she makes her first very own friend, and finds out that there are others who also weren't meant for the life they lead.<br />Like Pepper and Blue, both genetically edited: one to work in factories sorting and repairing discarded thecnical devices until they vanish, raised first by unfeeling robot "mothers", then by Owl, a spaceship's AI, with whom she flees this harrible planet; the other designed to become part of the same planet's elite but perfect enough for his speech impediment.<br /><br />There are many crucial moments in this book that one day humankind might have to face in daily life, such as: Do you really have to feel cheated when an AI clearly passing the Turing Test befriends you but hasn't "come out" to you about what they are right away? If you gene-tweak a population, are they then your product to do with as you please? And can you be allowed to sell and buy AIs at all?<br />Other than in many books dealing with the "uncanny valley" and AIs passing the Turing Test, Chambers allows to let the reader see multiple perspectives on theh topic: not only that of the AI's "caretakers" who are quite prepared to accept it as a person, not only that of the unknowing outsider who has to sort their feelings out once they are let in on the secret and find whether they can deal with it - but also from the point of view of the AI who never asked for any of this and has to deal with it anyway, or be deleted. Sidra's struggle with who she is is so very "human" that the reader cannot but feel with her.<br />Of course, the reader also feels with Pepper who is basically one of Huxley's ananymous work forces who never get a word in within Brave New World, one the underdogs of her home world. And she also is a Robinson Crusoe, stranded in a world of junk and aggressive dogs, building herself a float to leave her island and see the stars. The difference being, her Friday is inbuilt into her float. It is amazing to see how this sad little runaway grows into the tough, outgoing techy the reader sees taking care of Sidra - all thanks to being raised by an AI herself who didn't even have a body. Pepper's pain in loosing Owl because others fail to recognise her as a person and thus discard her as tech-trash is real, as real as the crew's grief upon Lovey's death. <br /><br />In the end, Sidra manages to find her place in Port Coriol, together with Owl who is reunited with her adoptive daughter Pepper - who never gave up looking for her.<br /><br />I find that I can't explain the thoughtful magic of this book properly. It has to be read and engulf the reader on its own. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11695081910979998278" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2027515654" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2027515654" />
    <a title="Evelina | AvalinahsBooks" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13716524-evelina-avalinahsbooks"><img alt="Evelina | AvalinahsBooks" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592760668p2/13716524.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2027515654?book_show_action=true">Jun 22, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Evelina | AvalinahsBooks" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Evelina | AvalinahsBooks" href="/user/show/13716524-evelina-avalinahsbooks">Evelina | AvalinahsBooks</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13716524-evelina-avalinahsbooks?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13716524-evelina-avalinahsbooks?shelf=books-of-2017">books-of-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13716524-evelina-avalinahsbooks?shelf=human-relationships">human-relationships</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2027515654" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1273326900277599831"><i><b>I have this complicated relationship with sequels somehow.</b> </i>I don't know why it's always like this. I mean, I'm not saying that <i>
  <b>all sequels</b>
</i> are bad. Of course not!<br/> <br/><i>
  <b>I'm not even saying this one is.</b>
</i><br/> <br/>But I was just kind of hoping it would be better.<br/> <br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1464977060ra/19300180.gif' width='253' height='210' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>(If the images don’t load, read this post <a href='http://avalinahsbooks.space/a-closed-and-common-orbit/?utm_source=Goodreads&utm_medium=Review&utm_campaign=A%20Closed%20And%20Common%20Orbit&utm_content=Evening%20review' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>here on my blog</a>)<br/> <br/>That is to say, it's still a solid three stars. But after <b>
  <i><a href='http://avalinahsbooks.space/a-long-way-to-a-small-angry-planet/?utm_source=Goodreads&utm_medium=Review&utm_campaign=A%20Closed%20And%20Common%20Orbit&utm_content=Evening%20review' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>A Long Way To A Small, Angry Planet</a>, </i>
</b>I just… don't know what I expected. I mean, <i>
  <b>I knew I wouldn't really be reading anoth</b></i></span>
  <span id="freeText1273326900277599831" style="display:none"><i><b>I have this complicated relationship with sequels somehow.</b> </i>I don't know why it's always like this. I mean, I'm not saying that <i>
  <b>all sequels</b>
</i> are bad. Of course not!<br> <br><i>
  <b>I'm not even saying this one is.</b>
</i><br> <br>But I was just kind of hoping it would be better.<br> <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1464977060ra/19300180.gif" width="253" height="210" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>(If the images don’t load, read this post <a href="http://avalinahsbooks.space/a-closed-and-common-orbit/?utm_source=Goodreads&amp;utm_medium=Review&amp;utm_campaign=A%20Closed%20And%20Common%20Orbit&amp;utm_content=Evening%20review" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">here on my blog</a>)<br> <br>That is to say, it's still a solid three stars. But after <b>
  <i><a href="http://avalinahsbooks.space/a-long-way-to-a-small-angry-planet/?utm_source=Goodreads&amp;utm_medium=Review&amp;utm_campaign=A%20Closed%20And%20Common%20Orbit&amp;utm_content=Evening%20review" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">A Long Way To A Small, Angry Planet</a>, </i>
</b>I just… don't know what I expected. I mean, <i>
  <b>I knew I wouldn't really be reading another book about the wonderful crew of the Wayfarer</b>
</i> that just runs away with your entire heart and soul. No, those hopes have been crushed ever since I heard about this one properly coming out (I mean, upon finding out that <i>
  <b>it's not</b>
</i> about the Wayfarer), but… you know. <i>
  <b>One stupidly keeps hoping.</b>
</i><br> <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1464282627ra/19223141.gif" width="351" height="198" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br> <br><i>
  <b>Viewed as a standalone, this is not a bad book at all.</b>
</i> We get to hear about the new Lovelace <i>(Sidra, I love that name, by the way)</i> and how her life is turning out. The struggles she goes through being something she wasn't meant to be. and all her soul-searching. <i>
  <b>Another great thing is hearing about Pepper’s childhood!</b>
</i> Sidra and Pepper's stories are told separately and eventually brought together, and the ending is just adorable!<br> <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1498158404ra/23101370.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br> <br><i>
  <b>But. I still could not grasp the spark.</b>
</i> There were a few things I wasn't too happy about, and since I'm such a nerd, I'll just give you a list.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1498158404ra/23101371.gif" width="309" height="172" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br> <br><b>First: where are all the species?</b><br> <br>If you remember the first book... It was plain <i>
  <b>swarming</b>
</i> with Aandrisks, Aeluons, Sianat pairs and all the like. This one? Mostly humans. We have one Aeluon secondary character. A few cameos by the other people. Honestly, Sianat pairs are not even mentioned <i>
  <b>once</b>
</i> throughout the book (I retain my right to have missed it! Although I doubt it.) <i>
  <b>...Where is everyone?</b>
</i><br> <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1498158404ra/23101372.gif" width="379" height="213" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br> <br><b>Second: I didn't love the characters.</b><br> <br>The charm of the first book mostly lay in the characters. In this one though? I can't say I really loved any of them. Sidra, the main character, seemed cold and offhand, at times just childish. Maybe she was meant to come across like that because she's an AI, and one fresh out of the box? But neither Owl nor Lovey ever was like that, although they're also AI. I also felt Pepper's character to be sort of flat. She was annoyed with someone for half the book. I know she's had it tough. But she didn't appear quite like that in the first book.<br> <br><b>Third: plot =/= spark?</b><br> <br>I will admit that this book had <i>
  <b>actually more plot</b>
</i> than A Long Way! But even so, it just.. didn't do it for me. It's still a three stars for sure, but it just sort of passed me by. Comparing it to the blazing trail the first book left, like a comet passing through, <i>
  <b>this one would just qualify as a blink and a whimper.</b>
</i><br> <br><i><b>All in all, I don't regret reading it,</b> </i>and I will probably read the third one, as I hear it's coming up. But I know I won't read quite another book like <b>
  <i>A Long Way</i>
</b> anytime soon. <i>
  <b>Some masterpieces are impossible to repeat.<br> <br><a href="http://avalinahsbooks.space/a-closed-and-common-orbit/?utm_source=Goodreads&amp;utm_medium=Review&amp;utm_campaign=A%20Closed%20And%20Common%20Orbit&amp;utm_content=Evening%20review" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Read Post On My Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/avalinahsbooks/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">My Bookstagram</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/AvalinahsBooks" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Bookish Twitter</a></b>
</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="1273326900277599831" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer18287343831040306497">I think I liked this stand-alone followup to <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22733729.The_Long_Way_to_a_Small__Angry_Planet__Wayfarers___1_' title='The Long Way to a Small, Angry Planet (Wayfarers, #1) by Becky Chambers' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Long Way to a Small, Angry Planet</a> even more than the first. The cast is much smaller, but because of this the reader is let in much more closely to a few unique lives - the AI formerly known as Lovey as she adjusts to living within a bodily form, and a small child named Jane who repairs scrap for robots. There are many comments about humanity and identity, destruction of natural environments, autonomy, and friendship. </span>
  <span id="freeText18287343831040306497" style="display:none">I think I liked this stand-alone followup to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22733729.The_Long_Way_to_a_Small__Angry_Planet__Wayfarers___1_" title="The Long Way to a Small, Angry Planet (Wayfarers, #1) by Becky Chambers" rel="nofollow noopener">The Long Way to a Small, Angry Planet</a> even more than the first. The cast is much smaller, but because of this the reader is let in much more closely to a few unique lives - the AI formerly known as Lovey as she adjusts to living within a bodily form, and a small child named Jane who repairs scrap for robots. There are many comments about humanity and identity, destruction of natural environments, autonomy, and friendship. </span>

<div id="review_1742412408" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1742412408" />
    <a title="William" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36549125-william"><img alt="William" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593268986p2/36549125.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1742412408?book_show_action=true">Feb 19, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="William" class="user" itemprop="url" name="William" href="/user/show/36549125-william">William</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/29808780-a-closed-and-common-orbit">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36549125-william?shelf=extraordinary-books">extraordinary-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1742412408" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10981044754415026797"><b>5 Full Stars. A total joy. </b> Her very best book of all.<br/><br/>So full of heart and love and a deep understanding of what it means to be human, and to become human. Ms. Chambers is a joy. Her writing expresses what we feel inside, the hidden truths, the mystery. <b>The Long Way...</b> is also so full of heart and joy and friendship, and <b>A Closed and Common Orbit</b> carries this forward.<br/><br/>This is a tale of the very young Jane who becomes Pepper, and Lovelace who becomes Sidra. Their stories are interwoven, and in man</span>
  <span id="freeText10981044754415026797" style="display:none"><b>5 Full Stars. A total joy. </b> Her very best book of all.<br><br>So full of heart and love and a deep understanding of what it means to be human, and to become human. Ms. Chambers is a joy. Her writing expresses what we feel inside, the hidden truths, the mystery. <b>The Long Way...</b> is also so full of heart and joy and friendship, and <b>A Closed and Common Orbit</b> carries this forward.<br><br>This is a tale of the very young Jane who becomes Pepper, and Lovelace who becomes Sidra. Their stories are interwoven, and in many ways reflect each other across time and space. They are struggling to survive and grow and learn to love.<br><br>The young Jane faces almost insurmountable difficulties in becoming Pepper, and in becoming Pepper and Blue together.<br><br>The AI Lovelace is given a gift of love by Pepper, a chance to become a truly independent person, and to grow out of "programming" and into freedom. <br><br>The pace is slow and thoughtful at first, and then more intense in the past and the present of the book, in parallel. And as the pace increases, so do the thoughts of what it means to be human, and the responsibilities we take on when we begin to love.<br><br>Some might see this as a lovely little space opera, but the author gently encourages us to feel the realities of our lives; it is far more than a little space opera.<br><br>In <b>A Closed and Common Orbit</b>, we see the common orbit of hearts growing towards each other. Wonderful.<br><br>Becky Chambers<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1597929757i/29992624._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><a href="http://ichef.bbci.co.uk/images/ic/640x360/p04dygv3.jpg" target="blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Full size image here</a><br><br>Notes:<br>4.0% "Holy crap this is WRONG. "Already, Sidra preferred Coriol’s dark side. It was a curious astronomical phenomenon –a planet tidally locked with its sun, a moon tidally locked with its planet, each with a day and night that never shifted across their respective surfaces.""<br><br> 54.0% "Very different from "Long Way..." but very good. Really enjoying it a lot"<br> <br> 79.0% "Wonderful. Better and better each page. <br><i>"Life is terrifying. None of us have a rule book. None of us know what we’re doing here. So, the easiest way to stare reality in the face and not utterly lose your shit is to believe that you have control over it."</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="10981044754415026797" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2443285479" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16026799374239423590">3.5 to 4 stars<br/><br/>I have previously referred to books like A Closed and Common Orbit as transition books. What I mean by this is that it is the middle book in a trilogy that seems to me more of a transition between the first and last book than a stand-alone story. I suppose it doesn’t have to be the middle book in a trilogy – it could be any book in a series that does have that major-build-up-to-a-climax stand-alone feel. But, if you completely left it out, the next book may not make quite as much s</span>
  <span id="freeText16026799374239423590" style="display:none">3.5 to 4 stars<br /><br />I have previously referred to books like A Closed and Common Orbit as transition books. What I mean by this is that it is the middle book in a trilogy that seems to me more of a transition between the first and last book than a stand-alone story. I suppose it doesn’t have to be the middle book in a trilogy – it could be any book in a series that does have that major-build-up-to-a-climax stand-alone feel. But, if you completely left it out, the next book may not make quite as much sense. That all being said, you can probably tell by now that I was not particularly wowed by this book, but I appreciate it as part of the narrative.<br /><br />Now, the next thing I noticed was, while I remembered some of the basic plot points of the first book, it is not one that stuck with me much. Because of this, getting into it at first was a bit difficult, but I did end up finding the plot and characters to be interesting. I think that the best way to explain is that it is a commentary on prejudice and class structure, but told in a sci-fi setting with aliens, AI, and genetically engineered clone humans being the main subjects. So, at times throughout the narrative it would stop there would be a conversation between two characters about their treatment when around another alien race. Or, their will be a discussion about the background of a character starting off AI and trying to me more human, etc. While at times you hate for a break in the action, I remember this from the first book, and I think it is one of the cool things about this authors approach to this series. It definitely makes it unique.<br /><br />If you read the first book and enjoyed it, give this one a shot. From my experience, it may be better to move on to this one sooner after finishing the first one than I did!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16026799374239423590" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1895539851" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1895539851" />
    <a title="Helene Jeppesen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21992464-helene-jeppesen"><img alt="Helene Jeppesen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528006866p2/21992464.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1895539851?book_show_action=true">Feb 04, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Helene Jeppesen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Helene Jeppesen" href="/user/show/21992464-helene-jeppesen">Helene Jeppesen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1895539851" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7746218297622575850">It was fun to be back in this unique, humorous sci-fi world that Becky Chambers has created with her first novel "The Small Way to a Long Angry Planet". Like many other people, I loved that first novel and was intrigued to dive into this companion one. It has to be said, though, that "A Closed and Common Orbit" is very different in both its plot as well as its tone of voice. To start with, it is more serious and doesn't have as much humour in it as we get in the first book. Also, it doesn't deal</span>
  <span id="freeText7746218297622575850" style="display:none">It was fun to be back in this unique, humorous sci-fi world that Becky Chambers has created with her first novel "The Small Way to a Long Angry Planet". Like many other people, I loved that first novel and was intrigued to dive into this companion one. It has to be said, though, that "A Closed and Common Orbit" is very different in both its plot as well as its tone of voice. To start with, it is more serious and doesn't have as much humour in it as we get in the first book. Also, it doesn't deal with a variety of characters as we mainly focus on two characters and their two POVs. <br />I still liked this book and was very much engrossed in especially Jane's life (without spoiling anything). Jane was innocent and so interesting to follow in her observations as she grows up. She was endearing and identifiable, and I couldn't help but love her and the dramatic changes that she goes through. I did feel, though, that the novel as a whole lost me somewhere halfway when I felt like things were dragging a bit too much; maybe because I was missing more characters and more activity on that front. <br />It also didn't helt that I wasn't particularly interested to read about Sidra (which means half of the book!). BUT all in all, this was still a great read because Becky Chambers has created a unique story which still has an important focus on how different we all are and how we should still be able to accept each other - no matter the species. I liked it, and I will never forget that Chambers was the author who REALLY got me into sci-fi. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7746218297622575850" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Trish" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3461034-trish"><img alt="Trish" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588663568p2/3461034.jpg" /></a>

        <a title="Trish" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Trish" href="/user/show/3461034-trish">Trish</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1957192106" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11053413516061521765"><b>4.5 stars</b>, but it's such a charming story about love and friendship and creating one's own destiny that I rounded up<br/><br/>This second volume of the <i>Wayfarers</i> series takes place immediately after the events of the first: Lovey is gone, Lovelace wiped her memory banks (no ill intent, just a protocol everyone hoped wouldn't get triggered) and because it is too sad and painful for Jenks, she left the ship with Pepper, who still has the illegal body kit.<br/><br/>This book, then, is about how Lovelace (naming hersel</span>
  <span id="freeText11053413516061521765" style="display:none"><b>4.5 stars</b>, but it's such a charming story about love and friendship and creating one's own destiny that I rounded up<br /><br />This second volume of the <i>Wayfarers</i> series takes place immediately after the events of the first: Lovey is gone, Lovelace wiped her memory banks (no ill intent, just a protocol everyone hoped wouldn't get triggered) and because it is too sad and painful for Jenks, she left the ship with Pepper, who still has the illegal body kit.<br /><br />This book, then, is about how Lovelace (naming herself Sidra) tries to come to terms with the limitations of a body, no longer having her designed purpose, learning about life, people and everything, ... basically, it's a coming-of-age story but with an AI (teaching us what it is to be human in the process). <br />But there is a second level to this: the story of Pepper, who started life as Jane #23 (a clone in a factory where she served as a work slave) and how she ended up in her repair shop.<br /><br />I'll admit that after knowing the story wouldn't move forward in this per se, I was a bit reluctant. Add to that that my audio version also had a different narrator (which makes sense, but I liked the first one so much). <br />Nevertheless, considering the quality of the first volume and the fact that this is nominated for no less than a HUGO, I wanted to read it.<br /><br />In general, there were less quote-worthy parts in this than in the first. Less grave ones too, despite the revelations about where Pepper and Blue come from. After all, the scope is much smaller here. And while many events in Pepper's past were less than pleasant, there wasn't that much at stake since we already knew where she'd end up. Thus, this (like the first) was fluffy in its execution, which is nothing bad, not in the least (it's refreshing even, because most SF nowadays is dark and dystopian-like), while also being a bit less thrilling than the first. However, the quality of this book was wonderful again, with the characters all being distinct and realistic, the dialogues natural, real development for all, a great way of bringing the two story threads together, and the world-building was detailed and therefore working fantastically.<br /><br />Thus, my doubts were unfounded, the author certainly delivered. Although I still have to say that this was not as enjoyable as the first. Not quite. Maybe I was just missing Kizzy and Dr. Chef too much. *lol* There was just nothing too much out there, everything was more ... toned down. I don't need great explosions and stuff and this author is impeccable at making characters carry the story (time flew by while reading this), but there is characters and then there is CHARACTERS. ;)<br /><br />I'll leave you with a few quotes that touched me:<br /><i>"I don't require participation in order to be enjoying myself. Company and interesting input, That's all I need."<br /><br />"You should talk to a real person when you can, but it's okay to make yourself feel better with imagination, too."<br /><br />"Just because someone goes away doesn't mean you stop loving them."<br /><br />"Possessing knowledge and performing an action are two entirely different processes."<br /><br />It was a mean way to keep someone from running, tied up with an extra layer of "we really don't care, go ahead, starve out there, you're totally replaceable".<br /><br />"Life is terrifying. None of us have a rule book. None of us know what we're doing here. So, the easiest way to stare reality in the face and not utterly lose your shit is to believe that you have control over it."</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="11053413516061521765" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30279227-ts-chan?shelf=library-book">library-book</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2422359548" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer10926414690137984676"><b>4.5 stars.</b><br/>A short review.<br/><br/>I never thought there'll be such a thing called cosy science-fiction, but I believe A Closed and Common Orbit can be considered as such. Charming and beautifully written, this stand-alone sequel continues the trilogy's intimate narrative on social sciences and humanities. So full of heart and incredibly moving, it made me tear up numerous times without being heavy-handed, and felt like a warm hug on a cold, brittle day. <br/><br/>Similar to The Long Way to A Small, Angry Planet, t</span>
  <span id="freeText10926414690137984676" style="display:none"><b>4.5 stars.</b><br />A short review.<br /><br />I never thought there'll be such a thing called cosy science-fiction, but I believe A Closed and Common Orbit can be considered as such. Charming and beautifully written, this stand-alone sequel continues the trilogy's intimate narrative on social sciences and humanities. So full of heart and incredibly moving, it made me tear up numerous times without being heavy-handed, and felt like a warm hug on a cold, brittle day. <br /><br />Similar to The Long Way to A Small, Angry Planet, the story is character-centric instead of plot-driven. The difference is that instead of an ensemble cast, we have two non-linear POVs for the majority of the book. The connectivity of these two POVs is the shared theme between an artificial intelligence created to be a tool and an enhanced human 'clone' born and bred for cheap labour. Their story of going beyond their intended purpose was wonderfully empathetic and heartwarming.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10926414690137984676" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1802885283" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1802885283" />
    <a title="✨    jamieson   ✨" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7706640-jamieson"><img alt="✨    jamieson   ✨" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1499961431p2/7706640.jpg" /></a>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1802885283?book_show_action=true">Jul 24, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="✨    jamieson   ✨" class="user" itemprop="url" name="✨    jamieson   ✨" href="/user/show/7706640-jamieson">✨    jamieson   ✨</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=favourite-covers">favourite-covers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=2017-reads">2017-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7706640-jamieson?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1802885283" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11429318217381637928"><i>
  <blockquote>“She felt as though she could reach out to that little girl and pull her through the years. Look, she’d say. Look who you’re gonna be. Look where you’re gonna go." </blockquote>
</i><br/><br/>I read <i>The Long Way to a Small Angry Planet</i> late last year and absolutely <b>loved everything about it</b>. It's truly one of the most joyous and beautiful books I've ever read, and I loved the cast so much. <br/><br/><i>A Closed and Common Orbit</i> is a companion novel, and I was a little war about it because it features different characters and a diff</span>
  <span id="freeText11429318217381637928" style="display:none"><i>
  <blockquote>“She felt as though she could reach out to that little girl and pull her through the years. Look, she’d say. Look who you’re gonna be. Look where you’re gonna go." </blockquote>
</i><br><br>I read <i>The Long Way to a Small Angry Planet</i> late last year and absolutely <b>loved everything about it</b>. It's truly one of the most joyous and beautiful books I've ever read, and I loved the cast so much. <br><br><i>A Closed and Common Orbit</i> is a companion novel, and I was a little war about it because it features different characters and a different setting. I wasn't sure if I would enjoy the AI elements of it and the main character. <b>Turns out I had nothing to worry about. I loved A Closed and Common Orbit so much as well</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1501472142i/23461350.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote><br>(by <a href="ssuccubitch.tumblr.com" rel="nofollow noopener">ssuccubitch</a> on tumblr)<br><br>A Closed and Common Orbit follows Lovelace 2.0 (who renames herself Sidra) and Pepper as they navigate Sidra's new body kit and role in the world. It flips between Sidra's perspective in current time, and Peppers as a child. I worry about alternate chapters because I always tend to like one of the perspectives more then the other. With A Closed and Common Orbit it was actually pretty close! I think I did like Peppers chapters just a tiny shade more, but I really enjoyed both Pepper and Sidra's chapters and was invested in both the current and past time periods. <br><br>My favourite thing about these books is definitely the world. The galaxy that these people live in is the kind of one I want to live in too. I love the different kinds of aliens that populate this series, and the diversity of people racially and sexually. This world is my happy place, it's impossible not to read about these characters filled up with so many hopes and dreams, with stars in their eyes and purpose in their heart and not feel some kind of intense moving joy.<br><br><b>the characters</b> are incredibly real and complex. They feel like tangible people, and even though I haven't struggled with what some of them have done personally, the human concerns and worries that underpin their problems make their characters realistic. The characters, and these books in general, very much explore the human condition and how characters exist in their spaces and I personally really enjoy those themes. <b>Thematically this book held up for me much more then the first</b>. While I adored what the first book did, I liked the issues and discussion around personhood that A Closed and Common Orbit Explored. <br><br>The only reason I rate this lower then The Long Way to a Small Angry Planet is because I personally didn't like the characters <i>as much</i> and I missed some of the aspects of the first book that I loved - like the space travel and varying species. But, I do think this book is more exciting and fast paced then the first, and there is a greater emotional depth to the characters relationships so that counteracted what I missed from the first book. <b>This is definitely a very strong sequel that stands up on it's own</b><br><br><i>
  <blockquote>“Life is terrifying. None of us have a rule book. None of us know what we're doing here. So, the easiest way to stare reality in the face and not utterly lose your shit is to believe that you have control over it. "</blockquote>
</i><br><br>A Closed and Common Orbit picks up right where The Long Way to a Small Angry Planet left off and carries on the threads that were already established in the first book. This is true joyous sci-fi, with relatable characters who struggle everyday, but also try so hard to do their best and develop and grow in positive ways. Reading these is such a calming experience, and makes me feel happy and hopeful which I absolutely love. <br><br>Another 4.5 stars to Becky Chambers, she's a true genius and I love her so much for these books. Cannot wait for Record of a Spaceborn Few in 2018!</span>
  <a data-text-id="11429318217381637928" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1658966964" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1658966964" />
    <a title="Kai" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41788524-kai"><img alt="Kai" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1573562141p2/41788524.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1658966964?book_show_action=true">Jun 04, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kai" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kai" href="/user/show/41788524-kai">Kai</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=2017">2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1658966964" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13915674078889193671"><i>“Life is terrifying. None of us have a rule book. None of us know what we're doing here.”</i><br/><br/><b>2.5/5 Stars</b><br/><br/>I'm a huge fan of Wayfarers #1. It wasn't perfect but overall it was wonderful. I knew from experience that, going into Wayfarers #2, it wouldn't be the most exciting story ever. I'm afraid to say that it was downright boring, though.<br/><br/>I don't want to be mean or hurtful. I know that Becky Chamber's fans love this world she created, and so do I! The creativity behind all this is mindblowing. The work</span>
  <span id="freeText13915674078889193671" style="display:none"><i>“Life is terrifying. None of us have a rule book. None of us know what we're doing here.”</i><br /><br /><b>2.5/5 Stars</b><br /><br />I'm a huge fan of Wayfarers #1. It wasn't perfect but overall it was wonderful. I knew from experience that, going into Wayfarers #2, it wouldn't be the most exciting story ever. I'm afraid to say that it was downright boring, though.<br /><br />I don't want to be mean or hurtful. I know that Becky Chamber's fans love this world she created, and so do I! The creativity behind all this is mindblowing. The work and devotion that was put into these books is clear to see. But I still struggled with this second installment. For several reasons.<br /><br />This books is divided into two timelines, two characters. I connected with Jane, but not with Sidra. I even disliked Sidra sometimes. Jane's story was an exciting, frightening and emotional one. Sidra's was anything but. Worst of all however, Jane's story was cut short. Several important plot and character developements were completely left out, never to be elaborated any further. Or, you know, at all. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[For example: How did Pepper and Blue come to their names? How did they fall in love? What exactly happend on their journey, after they left their planet? So many details just got lost. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />For me there was so much more potential in Jane's story than in Sidra's. And while we're at it, let's talk about potential: this world she created is so vast, and so big and I wish she had focused on more than the four "main characters". That's what I loved about <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22733729.The_Long_Way_to_a_Small__Angry_Planet__Wayfarers___1_" title="The Long Way to a Small, Angry Planet (Wayfarers, #1) by Becky Chambers" rel="nofollow noopener">The Long Way to a Small, Angry Planet</a>: it was so rich of detail and diversity, the cast was big and they all had their own stories and their history. This book seemed a little grey in comparison.<br />Towards the end, everything suddenly moved too fast. The plot was rushed, forced into the last few chapters and solved even quicker than that. The book left me with feelings of disconnect and dissatisfaction. And while I initially wanted to give three stars, I might have to take yet another star away. The cover promised such a beautiful story, but it was an empty promise.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.instagram.com/fantasticbooksandwheretofindem/" rel="nofollow noopener">Find more of my books on Instagram</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="13915674078889193671" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('xUIxqYuHhPERihb75yvZfhBFNZsdbGlKTZPIWRj3/jk527CaX22o/K58slJzh7MGp/6GJKMtbbz1kPOfQBXpOQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('pz9mM6hlX09hsh/LwA6wxzP2M7hFqIodnNyNbw/S249bpucAfI9zQt5Eu2JUotq/hE2AB/vpjusk37apVzDMjw==')})
  }
//]]>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer6225363798136979244">Becky Chambers is a science fiction author based in Northern California. She is best known for her Hugo Award-winning Wayfarers series, which currently includes The Long Way to a Small, Angry Planet, A Closed and Common Orbit, and Record of a Spaceborn Few. Her books have also been nominated for the Arthur C. Clarke Award, the Locus Award, and the Women's Prize for Fiction, among others. Her most </span>
  <span id="freeText6225363798136979244" style="display:none">Becky Chambers is a science fiction author based in Northern California. She is best known for her Hugo Award-winning Wayfarers series, which currently includes The Long Way to a Small, Angry Planet, A Closed and Common Orbit, and Record of a Spaceborn Few. Her books have also been nominated for the Arthur C. Clarke Award, the Locus Award, and the Women's Prize for Fiction, among others. Her most recent work is To Be Taught, If Fortunate, a standalone novella.<br /><br />Becky has a background in performing arts, and grew up in a family heavily involved in space science. She spends her free time playing video and tabletop games, keeping bees, and looking through her telescope. Having hopped around the world a bit, she’s now back in her home state, where she lives with her wife. She hopes to see Earth from orbit one day.</span>
